  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7527a2e6-686f-4f16-9982-b9655612c376'
      });
    }

<div id="review_2315781316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315781316" />
    <a title="Kerri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27593845-kerri"><img alt="Kerri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571347984p2/27593845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315781316?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerri" href="/user/show/27593845-kerri">Kerri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781503943582" href="/book/show/32720346-paper-boats">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27593845-kerri?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27593845-kerri?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27593845-kerri?shelf=won-t-read-again">won-t-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27593845-kerri?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27593845-kerri?shelf=did-not-like-at-all">did-not-like-at-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315781316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2200953634644314996">Truly one of the most painful things I've read in awhile. Four hundred pages of characters being stupid, and "self-sacrificing" in the name of LOVE. Uh, sorry folks, that's not love. You don't marry someone because you don't want to break their heart. <br/><br/>Kugy, a girl who the author loves to repeatedly tell us is brave, and quirky, and doesn't care what anyone thinks, apparently cares A LOT what other people think, to the point where she does a ridiculous amount of hiding. Least brave heroine ever. </span>
  <span id="freeText2200953634644314996" style="display:none">Truly one of the most painful things I've read in awhile. Four hundred pages of characters being stupid, and "self-sacrificing" in the name of LOVE. Uh, sorry folks, that's not love. You don't marry someone because you don't want to break their heart. <br /><br />Kugy, a girl who the author loves to repeatedly tell us is brave, and quirky, and doesn't care what anyone thinks, apparently cares A LOT what other people think, to the point where she does a ridiculous amount of hiding. Least brave heroine ever. <br /><br />Keenan is a joke. Plenty of girls like him, and rather than saying, "No thanks, you're not really my type," he just goes along with them, acting like a boyfriend when he clearly has no interest in them. And then, out of guilt, he forces an interest in them. Poor Ludhe. <br /><br />I know this book’s first language isn't English, so perhaps some things got lost in translation, but there's a lot of of odd phrasing here. Characters laugh at what feels like inappropriate times. Jokes and dialogue fall flat. And towards the middle, practically every chapter ended with either Keenan or Kugy proclaiming that they'd "moved on", putting the other behind them. Except, they never did. Hence the melodrama. If this book had been two hundred pages shorter, the story may have been interesting, but the other half was filled with unnecessary drama that really added nothing, other than a desire to tear my own hair out. I definitely won't be picking this book up again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2200953634644314996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2667391473" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6206094-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440416770p2/6206094.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2667391473?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/6206094-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781503943582" href="/book/show/32720346-paper-boats">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2667391473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13527720794730473030">(Kindle)<br/><br/>A sweet story about Kugi and Keenan, one a story teller and one a painter. Their path to becoming a couple is complicated. The childlike hope of telling fairy tales and painting for a living clash with a reality to have a career, a job and a paycheck.<br/><br/>The transition from childhood to adulthood while maintaining childlike creativity, joy and hope is a bumpy struggle.<br/><br/>Conflict happens when parental expectations, assumptions and well-meaning friends complicate things further. <br/><br/>The main charact</span>
  <span id="freeText13527720794730473030" style="display:none">(Kindle)<br /><br />A sweet story about Kugi and Keenan, one a story teller and one a painter. Their path to becoming a couple is complicated. The childlike hope of telling fairy tales and painting for a living clash with a reality to have a career, a job and a paycheck.<br /><br />The transition from childhood to adulthood while maintaining childlike creativity, joy and hope is a bumpy struggle.<br /><br />Conflict happens when parental expectations, assumptions and well-meaning friends complicate things further. <br /><br />The main characters cause trouble for themselves by not speaking up, not listening to their hearts, staying too long "in the moment" and missing opportunities to settle things. The author seems unwilling to let her main characters suffer too much, though and creates secondary romantic partners that are shadows of the main love interest. In any other story the secondary romances would have been the headliners.<br /><br />Paper Boats gets it's name from the origami boats that Kugi sends to the ocean, to King Neptune, sharing her hopes, dreams, worries and wishes. It's a "meet cute" kind of gimmick.<br /><br />Recommend--not a stressful read. Charming little love story.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13527720794730473030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11732923192382640599">I picked this up through one of those $2 credits on select books if you subscribe to some Amazon list and didn't expect much from it. I am so glad I picked it up. It is a different take on the romance genre, at least for me - someone who doesn't typically read romance. It is well written and feels authentic, though it's not a depiction of a dating culture I'm familar with. This is a light, warm, beach read for a bright little pick-me-up, which is exactly what I was looking for. Koogi and Keenan </span>
  <span id="freeText11732923192382640599" style="display:none">I picked this up through one of those $2 credits on select books if you subscribe to some Amazon list and didn't expect much from it. I am so glad I picked it up. It is a different take on the romance genre, at least for me - someone who doesn't typically read romance. It is well written and feels authentic, though it's not a depiction of a dating culture I'm familar with. This is a light, warm, beach read for a bright little pick-me-up, which is exactly what I was looking for. Koogi and Keenan are weird in a way I understand and passionate in a way I admire. There is so much beauty in these characters and their story, it captivated me until the end. I think their love story is one I will remember for quite awhile.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253640298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5423533515176467942">This books is beautiful beyond words. In its joy, but also in its heartache. Who hasn’t known what it’s like to waiver between dream and reality? Love and duty? Desire and responsibility? These characters walk a tightrope full of universal questions. It is all too easy to relate as we take the loving, and sometimes painful, journey with them. Life isn’t as simple as finding your soulmate. It rests precariously on the choices that either move you closer to that future together, or keep you apart </span>
  <span id="freeText5423533515176467942" style="display:none">This books is beautiful beyond words. In its joy, but also in its heartache. Who hasn’t known what it’s like to waiver between dream and reality? Love and duty? Desire and responsibility? These characters walk a tightrope full of universal questions. It is all too easy to relate as we take the loving, and sometimes painful, journey with them. Life isn’t as simple as finding your soulmate. It rests precariously on the choices that either move you closer to that future together, or keep you apart — for whatever well-intended reasons. This book will resonate with all the dreamers out there — which I hope is all of us.</span>

<div id="review_1981904797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981904797" />
    <a title="Peggy Harris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7149068-peggy-harris"><img alt="Peggy Harris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464664150p2/7149068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981904797?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peggy Harris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peggy Harris" href="/user/show/7149068-peggy-harris">Peggy Harris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34619486-paper-boats">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7149068-peggy-harris?shelf=giveaways">giveaways</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981904797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15001286608021139144">I thought it didn't exist, but here it is! I found it. <b>The NEVERENDING STORY.</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494114211ra/22686404.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I don't know why I punished myself and read it all in a single day, but perhaps I was thinking that the story HAD to end sometime. <br/><br/>The book spans over a time period of four years. FOUR YEARS. <br/>Now don't get me wrong. This can be done and done well. In Anita Shreve's "The Last Time They Met," the story spanned throughout the characters' whole lives just about. But this book seemed to go on and on and you knew where it wa</span>
  <span id="freeText15001286608021139144" style="display:none">I thought it didn't exist, but here it is! I found it. <b>The NEVERENDING STORY.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494114211ra/22686404.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I don't know why I punished myself and read it all in a single day, but perhaps I was thinking that the story HAD to end sometime. <br><br>The book spans over a time period of four years. FOUR YEARS. <br>Now don't get me wrong. This can be done and done well. In Anita Shreve's "The Last Time They Met," the story spanned throughout the characters' whole lives just about. But this book seemed to go on and on and you knew where it was going to end up...but it just wouldn't get there. <br><br>Let's talk about the character's for a minute. None of them would say what they were feeling! It was a complete contradiction with Kugy because she was portrayed as an eccentric and weird character who didn't care what anyone thought of her. Yet here she was, not telling anyone her feelings and running away from them. It was completely unbelievable that she wouldn't even tell the girl who'd been her best friend her whole life what was going on. Keenan was the same way. It was enough to make you want to smack them. Several times. In the face.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494113611ra/22686364.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Each time Kugy and Keenan saw each other again, it was like they almost said how they felt....but nope, just couldn't do it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494120863ra/22686976.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kugy and Keenan run from their feelings and refuse to talk about how they feel. This is basically the whole plot of the story. Over time, a year or so, they both begin to have a relationship with other people. In my opinion these are some really messed up relationships. <br><br>Keenan starts seeing Lehde and gives her a carved wooden heart that he had made specifically for Kugy and had even put Kugy's initials on it. Almost as if saying, here, you aren't special enough for me to make something just for you. In much the same manner, Kugy gives her fiancé Remi a book of stories that she'd made for Keenan years ago...but in her case it was even worse! She left a letter/card in the book meant for Keenan and Remi found it! Kugy also tried to reenact an inside joke that she and Keenan had with Remi. To me these were unacceptable behaviors in a relationship. <br><br>Through the whole course of the story Keenan and Kugy remain googly eyed and star crossed over each other, but never once do they feel anger. For instance, why wasn't Kugy mad when Keenan just disappeared without telling anyone? Why wasn't she mad when he took her book of stories and used them for his inspiration without telling her or even asking her if she was ok with it? It was like oh hey, I love you, but I'm going to run off and use your work to gain some notoriety and money without telling you. And then when Kugy sees him again she's not even upset over this?? I'm confused.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451776901ra/17601772.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>To me the only real character that had any depth and believability was Luhde. She was the youngest character in the novel...but didn't act like it. She said what she wanted! She told people how she felt! She was refreshing and honest. Unlike Keenan and Kugy, she went after what she wanted! This was seen when she went by herself to Jakarta even though she'd never left Bali. She was wise beyond her years as well. In fact, most of the quotes I liked in this book came from her. Here's some of my favorite Luhde quotes:<br><br>"A canvas with nothing on it can speak volumes. And without nothingness, how would you start something new?"<br><br>"Memories are nothing but ghosts in the corners of our minds. They will always remain ghosts if we don't deal with them. They will never become reality."<br><br>"The heart doesn't choose to love. Love chooses the heart. So you see, when you say you've chosen me, you will never be able to truly love me. Because the heart doesn't need to choose--it always knows where to set down anchor and rest."<br><br>All in all I didn't hate the book...but I didn't like it either. I liked the premise of a girl leaving messages via paper boats for Neptune but this wasn't expanded upon enough in the novel. I thought that this could have been incorporated more in moving the plot forward. I wish that more of the characters could have been like Luhde. Luhde and Wayon were the two people that I felt the most for. They were both honest and kind. The other characters just left me feeling like I wanted to bash them in the head. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494122543ra/22687125.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15001286608021139144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1737439295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1737439295" />
    <a title="Nurul AK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50603473-nurul-ak"><img alt="Nurul AK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459432893p2/50603473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1737439295?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nurul AK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nurul AK" href="/user/show/50603473-nurul-ak">Nurul AK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50603473-nurul-ak?shelf=always-be-with-you">always-be-with-you</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1737439295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14157857739035094655">OKAY WHERE TO BEGIN WITH THIS BOOK.<br/><br/>This is one of my favorite book ever and I will always want this book.<br/>They also adapt this book into two-parts movies and the movies are as perfect as the book can be. <br/><br/>This book centers around two young people each with different hobbies and ambitions. They are the epitome of their own dreams. The girl likes to write and the boy likes to draw. Together they dream to make their own story book. They would complete each other. But sometimes the reality is not goin</span>
  <span id="freeText14157857739035094655" style="display:none">OKAY WHERE TO BEGIN WITH THIS BOOK.<br /><br />This is one of my favorite book ever and I will always want this book.<br />They also adapt this book into two-parts movies and the movies are as perfect as the book can be. <br /><br />This book centers around two young people each with different hobbies and ambitions. They are the epitome of their own dreams. The girl likes to write and the boy likes to draw. Together they dream to make their own story book. They would complete each other. But sometimes the reality is not going the way they plan it to.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Karena hanya bersama kamu, segalanya terasa dekat, segala sesuatunya ada, segala sesuatunya benar. Dan Bumi hanyalah sebutir debu di bawah telapak kaki kita."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Because only with you, everything is at a good distance, everything is here, everything feels right. And the earth is just a speck of dust beneath our feet."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br /><br /><b>Plot</b><br />The plot is very very impressive. It's tense and romantic and depressing at its own way. I read this book around 8 or 9 years ago and I remember reading it in one go.<br />Series of event and conflicts happen throughout the story and left unresolved until at least a few chapters. It will get so intense at some point. I cant really say the plot is that fast-paced type because it can be said that this is a romance novel and the author tries to play the emotion games and ask the readers to get drawn and feel the problem the main characters are facing.<br /><br /><b>Writing</b><br />One of the impressive thing about this novel is how the author put a date in every sub chapters. It felt like we are following the MC’s life and the readers will be left surprised at how long they know each other, how long they have been facing the same issues and how long they have been living their life imperfectly, separatedly but connected at some ways. The reader will see that the events happened in the novel is not only happening in one night or one month. The details of time plays an important part in how the readers see what the MC have been through and how each event built their characters and expanded their ideas about dreams and future.<br /><br /><b>Character</b><br />The two MC are so good and interesting. Kugy and Keenan. They are just too humane. There are also other characters, Noni, Eko, Wanda, Luhde, Remi. They met, they had friends, they loved, they made mistakes, they cried, they left, they lost hope, they gave up. We will not see a knight in shining armor or a princess in glass shoes. They are the basic form of normal Indonesian teenager. They just have so many weaknesses. As the other romance stories, there are parts where it is too unreal and dramatic such as the the slipped moments, the almost-being-together-but-we-missed moment, the misunderstanding that make the two main character’s grew apart and other cheesy lines. But personally that’s what made me burst into tears. It’s just so heartbreaking. <br /><br /><b>Moral Lesson</b><br />I can’t say that it’s a really a moral lesson but the book is basically teaching us about never stop chasing your dreams even if it’s the impossible ones. If you put your heart into it, there will be a way. But sometimes, life demands us to be as realistic as possible and it wont always go the way we want. If that time comes there will be two or more choices, whether you want to stick to your dream and its path or you want to go the way life takes you to.<br />The author just takes the very simple and dreamy issue of my country. The story is just so traditional yet so real and even if it’s added with romance stuffs, the basic theme of this story is just amazing.<br /><br />Overall, this novel is very sweet. That kind of book you want to read all over again while drinking tea in rainy days. The setting of the story also took place in some of my favorite cities in Indonesia and it’s just added another star and point from me.<br /><br />Here is the movie trailer and the ost<br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vFjTDMJam30" rel="nofollow noopener">Perahu Kertas Trailer</a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mAR13pqouhc" rel="nofollow noopener">Perahu Kertas Ost</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14157857739035094655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026480202" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2458736919656965867">Personally I thought this book was awful. Kugy has a boyfriend Josh whom we almost never hear about and certainly aren't given any reason to care about. She tortures herself over Keenan and it was super annoying. Why not just break up with your boyfriend whom you are giving no attention and be with the guy you're totally obsessed with? So annoying. It would be different if it had been written in such a way that the reader cared about Josh. But there was no tension there and no reason for her to </span>
  <span id="freeText2458736919656965867" style="display:none">Personally I thought this book was awful. Kugy has a boyfriend Josh whom we almost never hear about and certainly aren't given any reason to care about. She tortures herself over Keenan and it was super annoying. Why not just break up with your boyfriend whom you are giving no attention and be with the guy you're totally obsessed with? So annoying. It would be different if it had been written in such a way that the reader cared about Josh. But there was no tension there and no reason for her to be with him. Everyone unrealistically falls in love so easily. Everyone is described as perfect or quirky and bam in love. In the end they were both willing to be with someone else because those people didn't deserve to be hurt. Um yeah because marrying someone while you're obsessively in love with someone else is totally what they deserve... thankfully those good people who they would've married had the good sense to realize they didn't have their whole hearts and break it off. The characters were shallow. I wanted to finish the book to know what happens simply because I wanted to know the end. Not because I cared in the least. This is the most negative review I've ever left and I can only think of one other book I've disliked as much as this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2458736919656965867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13677182286168657480">I really enjoyed this story. It was definitely one that kept me picking up my book every spare minute when I could read. I had it on my Kindle for a while before I read it (so many books, so little time) but one day I decided to go back and read something that I'd had for a while and I randomly picked this one.   <span id="freeText13677182286168657480" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this story. It was definitely one that kept me picking up my book every spare minute when I could read. I had it on my Kindle for a while before I read it (so many books, so little time) but one day I decided to go back and read something that I'd had for a while and I randomly picked this one. I'm really glad I did! <br /><br />This was probably one of the Amazon deals, or one of the free monthly choices for Prime members. I don't usually choose books that take place in a country with which I'm not familiar. I feel like I might not understand the book if I don't know anything about the country or the culture. Not true here. The characters are genuinely human in every way and that's completely relatable. Turns out I didn't need to know anything about Indonesia because people are just people regardless of the setting. <br /><br />I don't want to give away any spoilers so I will just say that I was kept guessing how things would turn out right to the very end. This could be a fun summer read or a "curl up on the couch" read this winter. No matter when you choose to read it, it's a story of the kind of love and partnership we all dream about.</span>

  <span id="freeText2514384263811836052" style="display:none"><strong>Better than LaLa Land</strong><br /><br />Similar story about dreamers, with a love triangle (or two) but these are the most delightful characters, complete with endearing quirks, family life (cousins, siblings and parents) and friend groups in addition to their dream of creating. <br /><br />They meet at college and instantly connect. I found myself very drawn to them, their dreams and their uniqueness. (Fellow aliens, as their friends refer to them.) They also have big hearts, and a common desire to do good in the world.<br /><br />Not familiar at all with Indonesia, I was at first put off by the names I couldn't pronounce (Kugy, for one) and foreign pop culture references. But the story definitely pulled me in, and by the end I couldn't put it down! <br /><br />I was on the edge of my proverbial seat, hoping against all hope that these two would reconnect. And yet...the next people they meet are even more desirable, if that's possible! <br /><br />My only wish was that the letters to Neptune (her paper boats) would play a stronger role in the story. </span>

  <span id="freeText11237952333752369771" style="display:none">Disclosure: I would like to thank Goodreads and Amazon for the copy of Paper Boats by Dee Lestari (translated by Tiffany Tsao).<br /><br />I gave this book 3 stars out of 5, which according to the goodreads scale means: “I liked it!” This was an enjoyable book to read, but not life changing. The characters are believable and their life stories and adventures, though complex, are believable. It is actually refreshing to read a romance novel where the characters go through multiple realistic problems. My struggle with this book was that the entire story was predictable. <br /><br />This story about finding yourself and your ultimate place in the world was sweet and realistic. We all face problems in life, and need to learn how to deal with situations. Throughout the book, the characters worked to achieve this. This theme was what kept me reading the book and hoping for the ending that I wished for these characters. <br /><br /></span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2113627109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2822256412769241610">“The Heart Wants What the Heart Wants.” Is the refrain I heard in my mind as I read Dee Lestari’s coming of age novel about two young people who met in college in Indonesia. Kugy the young woman is unique and so different from her friends at school. She is a talented writer of fairy tales, but feels that it is not a practical way to make a living so she only writes for herself. Keenan, the young man is an artist who wants to pursue his art, but his father wants him to take over the family busine</span>
  <span id="freeText2822256412769241610" style="display:none">“The Heart Wants What the Heart Wants.” Is the refrain I heard in my mind as I read Dee Lestari’s coming of age novel about two young people who met in college in Indonesia. Kugy the young woman is unique and so different from her friends at school. She is a talented writer of fairy tales, but feels that it is not a practical way to make a living so she only writes for herself. Keenan, the young man is an artist who wants to pursue his art, but his father wants him to take over the family business, telling him he must go to college for a degree that will help him step into his fathers place someday. When Kugy and Keenan meet there is a sense of kindred spirits, he loves her fairy tales and is inspired by them. She is filled with happiness when they are together, but their friends and families get in the way and their lives take different roads. Paper Boats is a wonderful heart touching story for teens to adults to read. I really enjoyed reading it…4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2822256412769241610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17179617288478023575" style="display:none">This Indonesian NA romance set at the turn of the millennium hit me right in the feels, complete with the ~struggling artist and complicated™ moments. It's told in multi POV so a lot of texture and context there, but I thought plot overstayed and overall story could have been shorter. There's the matter of it coming across as YA at times, so if that's not your thing... WHY NOT? Anyway, the friendship and family dramas can be relatable, and the '99~'03 nostalgic throwback can make the emotional cut even deeper. Also, this was a big hit so it was adapted into film (Perahu Kertas, 2013)—if anybody can point me to a proper stream, please? (It's not on Netflix! Excuse me??)<br /><br />P.S.   <span id="freeText14257304417539330141" style="display:none"><strong>Bittersweet with a happy ending...</strong><br /><br /> First loved the ending because it turned out the way I hoped...<br /><br />Secondly, I want to be a spy for Neptune, too! The female lead was amazingly weird, and I loved how she developed throughout. Yes, as we age, we sometimes have to give up dreams, but there are those rare few who know what they will be from the beginning and pursue it with all their heart, through trial and tribulations untold. <br /><br />It was a privilege to read this book when I won it from Goodreads. It introduced me to some new culture, and the character developments were well done, even though there were times I was aggravated from the lack of sharing. So, much angst would have been prevented if they had talked, but then, they wouldn't have ended up how they did. </span>

<div id="review_2250535513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2250535513" />
    <a title="Lauren Berger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4177823-lauren-berger"><img alt="Lauren Berger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541346585p2/4177823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2250535513?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Berger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Berger" href="/user/show/4177823-lauren-berger">Lauren Berger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34619486-paper-boats">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2250535513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16147998160190982636">I’m not sure I can put a finger on exactly what it is about this book that made me fall in love with it so deeply. Thirty pages in, I was hooked. Then my heart was systematically torn apart. I read the entirety of this book on a constant state of heartache. It made the characters even more relatable. If you’ve ever had a dream, you will find yourself in this characters. I found myself thinking about the story when I wasn’t reading. I threw the book down in exasperation at times. I found myself g</span>
  <span id="freeText16147998160190982636" style="display:none">I’m not sure I can put a finger on exactly what it is about this book that made me fall in love with it so deeply. Thirty pages in, I was hooked. Then my heart was systematically torn apart. I read the entirety of this book on a constant state of heartache. It made the characters even more relatable. If you’ve ever had a dream, you will find yourself in this characters. I found myself thinking about the story when I wasn’t reading. I threw the book down in exasperation at times. I found myself going back and picking out moments that stole my heart. I loved this book, so completely, despite it breaking my heart from the beginning. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16147998160190982636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10184339955865695680"><strong>insightful & refreshing</strong><br/><br/>This book handles its characters and their relationships with truly beautiful care, showing the link between the stories we tell about our lives and the way we live them. I enjoyed every page, and I particularly appreciated that the supporting cast was just as well-written and developed in their actions and roles as the main characters. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SCx3FIcTW5P2uUqRcSYvk4gWKOsdgB+HMAROlqO2A6BCFXY0YsB5aayUdOn12I6570AZ5esdm766mjDMvr6Btg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X9mqJFXxON7XxR9Mq8hIRJHfi8g+/PYuflsp/P06QN1V4KsEsCIaJI3oITQvNulu9om6xshhchf0xVem4DLCyw==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_1499340'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1499340.5_cm?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">5 cm<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/700880.Donny_Dhirgantoro?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Donny Dhirgantoro<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.86 avg rating &mdash; 14,129 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2005\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer4671400853978039001\">Bestseller book di Gramedia Bookstore selama 2 tahun berturut-turut!\n\nLima sahabat telah menjalin persahabatan selama tujuh tahun. Mereka adalah Arial yang paling tampan, Riani sebagai satu-satunya wanita dalam kelompok itu, Zafran yang berlagak sepe<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4671400853978039001\" style=\"display:none\">Bestseller book di Gramedia Bookstore selama 2 tahun berturut-turut!\n\nLima sahabat telah menjalin persahabatan selama tujuh tahun. Mereka adalah Arial yang paling tampan, Riani sebagai satu-satunya wanita dalam kelompok itu, Zafran yang berlagak seperti seorang penyair, Ian yang paling subur badannya, dan Genta yang dianggap sebagai leader dalam kelompok itu. Kegemaran mereka adalah mengeksekusi hal-hal yang tidak mungkin dan mencoba segala hal, mulai dari kafe paling terkenal di Jakarta, sampai nonton layar tancap. Semuanya penggemar film, dari film Hollywood sampai film yang nggak kelas—kecuali film India karena mereka punya prinsip bahwa semua persoalan di dunia atau masalah pasti ada jalan keluarnya, tapi bukan dalam bentuk joget.\n\nSuatu saat, karena terdorong oleh rasa bosan di antara satu dan yang lain, mereka memutuskan untuk tidak saling berkomunikasi dan bertemu satu sama lain selama tiga bulan. Selama tiga bulan berpisah itulah telah terjadi banyak hal yang membuat hati mereka lebih kaya dari sebelumnya. Pertemuan setelah tiga bulan yang penuh dengan rasa kangen akhirnya terjadi dan dirayakan dengan sebuah perjalanan. Sebuah perjalanan yang penuh dengan keyakinan, mimpi, cita-cita, dan cinta. Sebuah perjalanan yang telah mengubah mereka menjadi manusia sesungguhnya, bukan Cuma seonggok daging yang bisa berbicara, berjalan, dan punya nama.\n\n“Ada yang pernah bilang kalau idealisme adalah <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4941856639560238034">Dee Lestari, is one of the bestselling and critically acclaimed writers in Indonesia.<br/>Born in January 20, 1976, she began her debut with a serial novel: Supernova in 2001. Supernova’s first episode, <i>Kesatria, Putri, dan Bintang Jatuh</i> (The Knight, The Princess, and The Falling Star), was sold phenomenally, achieving a cult status among Indonesian young readers. She has published four other episodes:</span>
  <span id="freeText4941856639560238034" style="display:none">Dee Lestari, is one of the bestselling and critically acclaimed writers in Indonesia.<br />Born in January 20, 1976, she began her debut with a serial novel: Supernova in 2001. Supernova’s first episode, <i>Kesatria, Putri, dan Bintang Jatuh</i> (The Knight, The Princess, and The Falling Star), was sold phenomenally, achieving a cult status among Indonesian young readers. She has published four other episodes: <i>Akar</i> (The Root), <i>Petir</i> (The Lightning), <i>Partikel</i>(The Particle), and <i>Gelombang</i> (The Wave). <br />Aside of the Supernova series, Dee has also published a novel titled <i>Perahu Kertas</i> (Paper Boat), and three anthologies: <i>Filosofi Kopi</i> (Coffee’s Philosophy), <i>Madre</i>, and <i>Rectoverso</i> — a unique hybrid of music and literature. <br />Dee also has an extensive music career, producing four albums with her former vocal trio, and two solo albums. She has been writing songs for renowned Indonesian artists. <br /><i>Perahu Kertas</i> (Paper Boat) was turned into a movie in 2009, marking Dee’s debut as a screenplay writer. The movie became one of the national's block busters. Following the same path, <i>Madre, Filosofi Kopi, Madre,</i> and <i>Supernova KPBJ,</i> were made into movies. <br />In February 2016, Dee released the final episode of Supernova, <i>Inteligensi Embun Pagi</i> (Intelligence of the Morning Dew). All Dee’s books are published by Bentang Pustaka. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4941856639560238034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
